<li id="cite_note-DSM-5_definitions_+_addiction-dependence_distinction_+_Caffeine_use_disorder-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-DSM-5_definitions_+_addiction-dependence_distinction_+_Caffeine_use_disorder_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DSM-5_definitions_+_addiction-dependence_distinction_+_Caffeine_use_disorder_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DSM-5_definitions_+_addiction-dependence_distinction_+_Caffeine_use_disorder_3-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DSM-5_definitions_+_addiction-dependence_distinction_+_Caffeine_use_disorder_3-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DSM-5_definitions_+_addiction-dependence_distinction_+_Caffeine_use_disorder_3-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DSM-5_definitions_+_addiction-dependence_distinction_+_Caffeine_use_disorder_3-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">American Psychiatric Association (2013). <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150815050402/http://www.dsm5.org/Documents/Substance%20Use%20Disorder%20Fact%20Sheet.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Substance-Related and Addictive Disorders"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://www.dsm5.org/documents/substance%20use%20disorder%20fact%20sheet.pdf" rel="nofollow">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 15 August 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 July</span> 2015</span>. <q>Substance use disorder in DSM-5 combines the DSM-IV categories of substance abuse and substance dependence into a single disorder measured on a continuum from mild to severe. ... Additionally, the diagnosis of dependence caused much confusion. Most people link dependence with "addiction" when in fact dependence can be a normal body response to a substance. ... DSM-5 will not include caffeine use disorder, although research shows that as little as two to three cups of coffee can trigger a withdrawal effect marked by tiredness or sleepiness. There is sufficient evidence to support this as a condition, however it is not yet clear to what extent it is a clinically significant disorder.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Substance-Related+and+Addictive+Disorders&amp;rft.pages=1-2&amp;rft.pub=American+Psychiatric+Publishing&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.au=American+Psychiatric+Association&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.dsm5.org%2Fdocuments%2Fsubstance%2520use%2520disorder%2520fact%2520sheet.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-CRC_Press-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-CRC_Press_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CRC_Press_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=qfrLBQAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA222" rel="nofollow"><i>Introduction to Pharmacology</i></a> (third ed.). </li>
<li id="cite_note-pmid15448977-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-pmid15448977_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-pmid15448977_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-pmid15448977_5-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-pmid15448977_5-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Juliano LM, Griffiths RR (October 2004). <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/6533BsxXt?url=http://neuroscience.jhu.edu/griffiths%20papers/CaffwdReview.2004.pdf" rel="nofollow">"A critical review of caffeine withdrawal: empirical validation of symptoms and signs, incidence, severity, and associated features"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Psychopharmacology</i>. <b>176</b> (1): 1–29. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1007%2Fs00213-004-2000-x" rel="nofollow">10.1007/s00213-004-2000-x</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15448977" rel="nofollow">15448977</a>. Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://neuroscience.jhu.edu/griffiths%20papers/CaffwdReview.2004.pdf" rel="nofollow">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 29 January 2012. <q>Results: Of 49 symptom categories identified, the following 10 fulfilled validity criteria: headache, fatigue, decreased energy/ activeness, decreased alertness, drowsiness, decreased contentedness, depressed mood, difficulty concentrating, irritability, and foggy/not clearheaded. In addition, flu-like symptoms, nausea/vomiting, and muscle pain/stiffness were judged likely to represent valid symptom categories. In experimental studies, the incidence of headache was 50% and the incidence of clinically significant distress or functional impairment was 13%. Typically, onset of symptoms occurred 12–24 h after abstinence, with peak intensity at 20–51 h, and for a duration of 2–9 days.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Psychopharmacology&amp;rft.atitle=A+critical+review+of+caffeine+withdrawal%3A+empirical+validation+of+symptoms+and+signs%2C+incidence%2C+severity%2C+and+associated+features&amp;rft.volume=176&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=1-29&amp;rft.date=2004-10&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2Fs00213-004-2000-x&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F15448977&amp;rft.aulast=Juliano&amp;rft.aufirst=LM&amp;rft.au=Griffiths%2C+RR&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fneuroscience.jhu.edu%2Fgriffiths%2520papers%2FCaffwdReview.2004.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-effects-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-effects_30-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-effects_30-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-effects_30-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Bolton, Sanford; Null, Gary (1981). <a class="external text" href="http://orthomolecular.org/library/jom/1981/pdf/1981-v10n03-p202.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Caffeine: Psychological Effects, Use and Abuse"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthomolecular_Psychiatry_(journal)" title="Orthomolecular Psychiatry (journal)">Orthomolecular Psychiatry</a></i>. <b>10</b> (3): 202–211.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Orthomolecular+Psychiatry&amp;rft.atitle=Caffeine%3A+Psychological+Effects%2C+Use+and+Abuse&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=202-211&amp;rft.date=1981&amp;rft.aulast=Bolton&amp;rft.aufirst=Sanford&amp;rft.au=Null%2C+Gary&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Forthomolecular.org%2Flibrary%2Fjom%2F1981%2Fpdf%2F1981-v10n03-p202.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Cog10-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cog10_31-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Nehlig A (2010). "Is caffeine a cognitive enhancer?". <i>Journal of Alzheimer's Disease</i>. 20 Suppl 1: S85–94. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.3233%2FJAD-2010-091315" rel="nofollow">10.3233/JAD-2010-091315</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20182035" rel="nofollow">20182035</a>. <q>Caffeine does not usually affect performance in learning and memory tasks, although caffeine may occasionally have facilitatory or inhibitory effects on memory and learning. Caffeine facilitates learning in tasks in which information is presented passively; in tasks in which material is learned intentionally, caffeine has no effect. Caffeine facilitates performance in tasks involving working memory to a limited extent, but hinders performance in tasks that heavily depend on this, and caffeine appears to improve memory performance under suboptimal alertness. Most studies, however, found improvements in reaction time. The ingestion of caffeine does not seem to affect long-term memory. ...  Its indirect action on arousal, mood and concentration contributes in large part to its cognitive enhancing properties.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Alzheimer%27s+Disease&amp;rft.atitle=Is+caffeine+a+cognitive+enhancer%3F&amp;rft.volume=20+Suppl+1&amp;rft.pages=S85-94&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.3233%2FJAD-2010-091315&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F20182035&amp;rft.aulast=Nehlig&amp;rft.aufirst=A&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Peripheral_and_central_ergogenic_effects-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Peripheral_and_central_ergogenic_effects_35-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Peripheral_and_central_ergogenic_effects_35-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Peripheral_and_central_ergogenic_effects_35-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Peripheral_and_central_ergogenic_effects_35-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Peripheral_and_central_ergogenic_effects_35-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Peripheral_and_central_ergogenic_effects_35-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Pesta DH, Angadi SS, Burtscher M, Roberts CK (December 2013). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3878772" rel="nofollow">"The effects of caffeine, nicotine, ethanol, and tetrahydrocannabinol on exercise performance"</a>. <i>Nutrition &amp; Metabolism</i>. <b>10</b> (1): 71. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1186%2F1743-7075-10-71" rel="nofollow">10.1186/1743-7075-10-71</a>. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3878772" rel="nofollow">3878772</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/24330705" rel="nofollow">24330705</a>. <q>Caffeine-induced increases in performance have been observed in aerobic as well as anaerobic sports (for reviews, see [26,30,31]). Trained athletes seem to benefit from a moderate dose of 5 mg/kg [32], however, even lower doses of caffeine (1.0–2.0 mg/kg) may improve performance [33]. Some groups found significantly improved time trial performance [34] or maximal cycling power [35], most likely related to a greater reliance on fat metabolism and decreased neuromuscular fatigue, respectively. Theophylline, a metabolite of caffeine, seems to be even more effective in doing so [36]. The effect of caffeine on fat oxidation, however, may only be significant during lower exercise intensities and may be blocked at higher intensities [37]. ... For both caffeine-naïve as well as caffeine-habituated subjects, moderate to high doses of caffeine are ergogenic during prolonged moderate intensity exercise [61]. ... In summary, caffeine, even at physiological doses (3–6 mg/kg), as well as coffee are proven ergogenic aids and as such – in most exercise situations, especially in endurance-type events – clearly work-enhancing [26]. It most likely has a peripheral effect targeting skeletal muscle metabolism as well as a central effect targeting the brain to enhance performance, especially during endurance events (see Table 1). Also for anaerobic tasks, the effect of caffeine on the CNS might be most relevant. ... Muendel et al. [93] found a 17% improvement in time to exhaustion after nicotine patch application compared to a placebo without affecting cardiovascular and respiratory parameters or substrate metabolism. In this sense, nicotine seems to exert similar effects as caffeine by delaying the development of central fatigue as impaired central drive is an important factor contributing to fatigue during exercise. ... The physiological effects of the above mentioned substances are well established. However, the ergogenic effect of some of the discussed drugs may be questioned and one has to consider the cohort tested for every specific substance. However, only caffeine has enough strength of evidence to be considered an ergogenic aid.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Nutrition+%26+Metabolism&amp;rft.atitle=The+effects+of+caffeine%2C+nicotine%2C+ethanol%2C+and+tetrahydrocannabinol+on+exercise+performance&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=71&amp;rft.date=2013-12&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3878772&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24330705&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1186%2F1743-7075-10-71&amp;rft.aulast=Pesta&amp;rft.aufirst=DH&amp;rft.au=Angadi%2C+SS&amp;rft.au=Burtscher%2C+M&amp;rft.au=Roberts%2C+CK&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3878772&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-pmid21058748-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-pmid21058748_36-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Bishop D (December 2010). "Dietary supplements and team-sport performance". <i>Sports Medicine</i>. <b>40</b> (12): 995–1017. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.2165%2F11536870-000000000-00000" rel="nofollow">10.2165/11536870-000000000-00000</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21058748" rel="nofollow">21058748</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Sports+Medicine&amp;rft.atitle=Dietary+supplements+and+team-sport+performance&amp;rft.volume=40&amp;rft.issue=12&amp;rft.pages=995-1017&amp;rft.date=2010-12&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.2165%2F11536870-000000000-00000&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F21058748&amp;rft.aulast=Bishop&amp;rft.aufirst=D&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-pmid21411838-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-pmid21411838_37-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Conger SA, Warren GL, Hardy MA, Millard-Stafford ML (February 2011). <li id="cite_note-Ergogenics-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Ergogenics_38-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Liddle DG, Connor DJ (June 2013). "Nutritional supplements and ergogenic AIDS". <i>Primary Care</i>. <b>40</b> (2): 487–505. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.pop.2013.02.009" rel="nofollow">10.1016/j.pop.2013.02.009</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/23668655" rel="nofollow">23668655</a>. <q>Amphetamines and caffeine are stimulants that increase alertness, improve focus, decrease reaction time, and delay fatigue, allowing for an increased intensity and duration of training ...<br/>Physiologic and performance effects<br/> • Amphetamines increase dopamine/norepinephrine release and inhibit their reuptake, leading to central nervous system (CNS) stimulation<br/> • Amphetamines seem to enhance athletic performance in anaerobic conditions 39 40<br/> • Improved reaction time<br/> • Increased muscle strength and delayed muscle fatigue<br/> • Increased acceleration<br/> • Increased alertness and attention to task</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Primary+Care&amp;rft.atitle=Nutritional+supplements+and+ergogenic+AIDS&amp;rft.volume=40&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=487-505&amp;rft.date=2013-06&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.pop.2013.02.009&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F23668655&amp;rft.aulast=Liddle&amp;rft.aufirst=DG&amp;rft.au=Connor%2C+DJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Cellular_basis-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cellular_basis_86-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Nestler EJ (December 2013). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3898681" rel="nofollow">"Cellular basis of memory for addiction"</a>. <i>Dialogues in Clinical Neuroscience</i>. <b>15</b> (4): 431–43. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3898681" rel="nofollow">3898681</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/24459410" rel="nofollow">24459410</a>. <q>DESPITE THE IMPORTANCE OF NUMEROUS PSYCHOSOCIAL FACTORS, AT ITS CORE, DRUG ADDICTION INVOLVES A BIOLOGICAL PROCESS: the ability of repeated exposure to a drug of abuse to induce changes in a vulnerable brain that drive the compulsive seeking and taking of drugs, and loss of control over drug use, that define a state of addiction. ... A large body of literature has demonstrated that such ΔFosB induction in D1-type NAc neurons increases an animal's sensitivity to drug as well as natural rewards and promotes drug self-administration, presumably through a process of positive reinforcement</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Dialogues+in+Clinical+Neuroscience&amp;rft.atitle=Cellular+basis+of+memory+for+addiction&amp;rft.volume=15&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.pages=431-43&amp;rft.date=2013-12&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3898681&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24459410&amp;rft.aulast=Nestler&amp;rft.aufirst=EJ&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3898681&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Human-caffeine_NAcc_neuroimaging-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Human-caffeine_NAcc_neuroimaging_87-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Miller PM (2013). "Chapter III: Types of Addiction". <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=5gRNl3oIwWEC&amp;pg=PA784" rel="nofollow"><i>Principles of addiction comprehensive addictive behaviors and disorders</i></a> (1st ed.). Elsevier Academic Press. p. 784. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-12-398361-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-12-398361-9">978-0-12-398361-9</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">11 July</span> 2015</span>. <q>Astrid Nehlig and colleagues present evidence that in animals caffeine does not trigger metabolic increases or dopamine release in brain areas involved in reinforcement and reward.  A single photon emission computed tomography (SPECT) assessment of brain activation in humans showed that caffeine activates regions involved in the control of vigilance, anxiety, and cardiovascular regulation but did not affect areas involved in reinforcement and reward.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Chapter+III%3A+Types+of+Addiction&amp;rft.btitle=Principles+of+addiction+comprehensive+addictive+behaviors+and+disorders&amp;rft.pages=784&amp;rft.edition=1st&amp;rft.pub=Elsevier+Academic+Press&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-12-398361-9&amp;rft.aulast=Miller&amp;rft.aufirst=PM&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D5gRNl3oIwWEC%26pg%3DPA784&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Paper_cited_by_preceding_book_ref-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Paper_cited_by_preceding_book_ref_88-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Nehlig A, Armspach JP, Namer IJ (2010). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3181952" rel="nofollow">"SPECT assessment of brain activation induced by caffeine: no effect on areas involved in dependence"</a>. <i>Dialogues in Clinical Neuroscience</i>. <b>12</b> (2): 255–63. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3181952" rel="nofollow">3181952</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20623930" rel="nofollow">20623930</a>. <q>Caffeine is not considered addictive, and in animals it does not trigger metabolic increases or dopamine release in brain areas involved in reinforcement and reward. ... these earlier data plus the present data reflect that caffeine at doses representing about two cups of coffee in one sitting does not activate the circuit of dependence and reward and especially not the main target area, the nucleus accumbens. ... Therefore, caffeine appears to be different from drugs of dependence like cocaine, amphetamine, morphine, and nicotine, and does not fulfil the common criteria or the scientific definitions to be considered an addictive substance.<sup>42</sup></q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Dialogues+in+Clinical+Neuroscience&amp;rft.atitle=SPECT+assessment+of+brain+activation+induced+by+caffeine%3A+no+effect+on+areas+involved+in+dependence&amp;rft.volume=12&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=255-63&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3181952&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F20623930&amp;rft.aulast=Nehlig&amp;rft.aufirst=A&amp;rft.au=Armspach%2C+JP&amp;rft.au=Namer%2C+IJ&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3181952&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Temple JL (June 2009). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2699625" rel="nofollow">"Caffeine use in children: what we know, what we have left to learn, and why we should worry"</a>. <i>Neuroscience and Biobehavioral Reviews</i>. <b>33</b> (6): 793–806. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.neubiorev.2009.01.001" rel="nofollow">10.1016/j.neubiorev.2009.01.001</a>. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2699625" rel="nofollow">2699625</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19428492" rel="nofollow">19428492</a>. <q>Through these interactions, caffeine is able to directly potentiate dopamine neurotransmission, thereby modulating the rewarding and addicting properties of nervous system stimuli.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Neuroscience+and+Biobehavioral+Reviews&amp;rft.atitle=Caffeine+use+in+children%3A+what+we+know%2C+what+we+have+left+to+learn%2C+and+why+we+should+worry&amp;rft.volume=33&amp;rft.issue=6&amp;rft.pages=793-806&amp;rft.date=2009-06&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC2699625&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F19428492&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.neubiorev.2009.01.001&amp;rft.aulast=Temple&amp;rft.aufirst=JL&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC2699625&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-ICD-10_F15.2-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ICD-10_F15.2_90-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ICD-10_F15.2_90-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://apps.who.int/classifications/icd10/browse/2015/en#/F15.2" rel="nofollow">"ICD-10 Version:2015"</a>. World Health Organization. 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 July</span> 2015</span>. <q><br/>F15 Mental and behavioural disorders due to use of other stimulants, including caffeine ...<br/><br/>.2 Dependence syndrome<br/>A cluster of behavioural, cognitive, and physiological phenomena that develop after repeated substance use and that typically include a strong desire to take the drug, difficulties in controlling its use, persisting in its use despite harmful consequences, a higher priority given to drug use than to other activities and obligations, increased tolerance, and sometimes a physical withdrawal state.<br/>The dependence syndrome may be present for a specific psychoactive substance (e.g., tobacco, alcohol, or diazepam), for a class of substances (e.g., opioid drugs), or for a wider range of pharmacologically different psychoactive substances. [Includes:]<br/>Chronic alcoholism<br/>Dipsomania<br/>Drug addiction</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=ICD-10+Version%3A2015&amp;rft.pub=World+Health+Organization&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fapps.who.int%2Fclassifications%2Ficd10%2Fbrowse%2F2015%2Fen%23%2FF15.2&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-A1-DRD1_and_A2a-DRD2_review-130"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-A1-DRD1_and_A2a-DRD2_review_130-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-A1-DRD1_and_A2a-DRD2_review_130-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-A1-DRD1_and_A2a-DRD2_review_130-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Ferré S (2010). "Role of the central ascending neurotransmitter systems in the psychostimulant effects of caffeine". <i>Journal of Alzheimer's Disease</i>. 20 Suppl 1: S35–49. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.3233%2FJAD-2010-1400" rel="nofollow">10.3233/JAD-2010-1400</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20182056" rel="nofollow">20182056</a>. <q>By targeting A1-A2A receptor heteromers in striatal glutamatergic terminals and A1 receptors in striatal dopaminergic terminals (presynaptic brake), caffeine induces glutamate-dependent and glutamate-independent release of dopamine. These presynaptic effects of caffeine are potentiated by the release of the postsynaptic brake imposed by antagonistic interactions in the striatal A2A-D2 and A1-D1 receptor heteromers.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Alzheimer%27s+Disease&amp;rft.atitle=Role+of+the+central+ascending+neurotransmitter+systems+in+the+psychostimulant+effects+of+caffeine&amp;rft.volume=20+Suppl+1&amp;rft.pages=S35-49&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.3233%2FJAD-2010-1400&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F20182056&amp;rft.aulast=Ferr%C3%A9&amp;rft.aufirst=S&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Caffeine_psychostimulant_effects-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Caffeine_psychostimulant_effects_132-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Caffeine_psychostimulant_effects_132-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Bonaventura J, Navarro G, Casadó-Anguera V, Azdad K, Rea W, Moreno E, Brugarolas M, Mallol J, Canela EI, Lluís C, Cortés A, Volkow ND, Schiffmann SN, Ferré S, Casadó V (July 2015). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4500251" rel="nofollow">"Allosteric interactions between agonists and antagonists within the adenosine A2A receptor-dopamine D2 receptor heterotetramer"</a>. <i>Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America</i>. <b>112</b> (27): E3609–18. <a href="/wiki/Bibcode" title="Bibcode">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2015PNAS..112E3609B" rel="nofollow">2015PNAS..112E3609B</a>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1073%2Fpnas.1507704112" rel="nofollow">10.1073/pnas.1507704112</a>. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4500251" rel="nofollow">4500251</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/26100888" rel="nofollow">26100888</a>. <q>Adenosine A2A receptor (A2AR)-dopamine D2 receptor (D2R) heteromers are key modulators of striatal neuronal function. It has been suggested that the psychostimulant effects of caffeine depend on its ability to block an allosteric modulation within the A2AR-D2R heteromer, by which adenosine decreases the affinity and intrinsic efficacy of dopamine at the D2R.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Proceedings+of+the+National+Academy+of+Sciences+of+the+United+States+of+America&amp;rft.atitle=Allosteric+interactions+between+agonists+and+antagonists+within+the+adenosine+A2A+receptor-dopamine+D2+receptor+heterotetramer&amp;rft.volume=112&amp;rft.issue=27&amp;rft.pages=E3609-18&amp;rft.date=2015-07&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4500251&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F26100888&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1073%2Fpnas.1507704112&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F2015PNAS..112E3609B&amp;rft.aulast=Bonaventura&amp;rft.aufirst=J&amp;rft.au=Navarro%2C+G&amp;rft.au=Casad%C3%B3-Anguera%2C+V&amp;rft.au=Azdad%2C+K&amp;rft.au=Rea%2C+W&amp;rft.au=Moreno%2C+E&amp;rft.au=Brugarolas%2C+M&amp;rft.au=Mallol%2C+J&amp;rft.au=Canela%2C+EI&amp;rft.au=Llu%C3%ADs%2C+C&amp;rft.au=Cort%C3%A9s%2C+A&amp;rft.au=Volkow%2C+ND&amp;rft.au=Schiffmann%2C+SN&amp;rft.au=Ferr%C3%A9%2C+S&amp;rft.au=Casad%C3%B3%2C+V&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4500251&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Caffeine_SUD_interactions-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Caffeine_SUD_interactions_133-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Caffeine_SUD_interactions_133-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Ferré S (May 2016). <a class="external text" href="https://zenodo.org/record/1232639" rel="nofollow">"Mechanisms of the psychostimulant effects of caffeine: implications for substance use disorders"</a>. <i>Psychopharmacology</i>. <b>233</b> (10): 1963–79. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1007%2Fs00213-016-4212-2" rel="nofollow">10.1007/s00213-016-4212-2</a>. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4846529" rel="nofollow">4846529</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/26786412" rel="nofollow">26786412</a>. <q>The striatal A2A-D2 receptor heteromer constitutes an unequivocal main pharmacological target of caffeine and provides the main mechanisms by which caffeine potentiates the acute and long-term effects of prototypical psychostimulants.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Psychopharmacology&amp;rft.atitle=Mechanisms+of+the+psychostimulant+effects+of+caffeine%3A+implications+for+substance+use+disorders&amp;rft.volume=233&amp;rft.issue=10&amp;rft.pages=1963-79&amp;rft.date=2016-05&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4846529&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F26786412&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2Fs00213-016-4212-2&amp;rft.aulast=Ferr%C3%A9&amp;rft.aufirst=S&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fzenodo.org%2Frecord%2F1232639&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link <li id="cite_note-Ferre_2008-134"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Ferre_2008_134-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Ferre_2008_134-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Ferre_2008_134-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Ferre_2008_134-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Ferré S (2008). "An update on the mechanisms of the psychostimulant effects of caffeine". <i>J. Neurochem</i>. <b>105</b> (4): 1067–1079. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1111%2Fj.1471-4159.2007.05196.x" rel="nofollow">10.1111/j.1471-4159.2007.05196.x</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18088379" rel="nofollow">18088379</a>. <q>On the other hand, our 'ventral shell of the nucleus accumbens' very much overlaps with the striatal compartment simply described by De Luca et al. (2007) as 'nucleus accumbens shell,' where both studies show that caffeine does not modify the extracellular levels of dopamine. Therefore, the results of both experimental groups are basically the same and point to differential effects of caffeine in different striatal subcompartments. In fact, analyzing the effects of the intrastriatal perfusion of an A1 receptor antagonist in several other striatal compartments showed striking differences compared with the shell of the nucleus accumbens. Thus, A1 receptor blockade significantly increased the extracellular concentration of dopamine, but not glutamate, in the core of the nucleus accumbens and in the caudate–putamen and the effect was more pronounced in the most medial compartments (Boryczet al. 2007). In summary, a subregional difference in the A1 receptor-mediated control of glutamate and dopamine release exists in the striatum ... A2A receptors play a crucial role in the sleep-promoting effects of adenosine and the arousal-enhancing effects of caffeine (Huang et al. 2007; Ferré et al. 2007a). Those A2A receptors are localized in the ventrolateral pre-optic area of the hypothalamus and their stimulation promotes sleep by inducing GABA release in the histaminergic tuberomammillary nucleus, thereby inhibiting the histaminergic arousal system ... chronic caffeine exposure counteracts both motor activation and dopamine release in the nucleus accumbens induced by caffeine or an A1 receptor antagonist ... An additional factor that might play a significant role in caffeine tolerance is the significant increase in plasma and extracellular concentrations of adenosine with chronic caffeine exposure ... The existence of an A1 receptor-mediated glutamate-independent modulation of dopamine release suggested the presence of functional A1 receptors in striatal dopaminergic terminals. ... In the SSM, adenosine acts pre- and post-synaptically through multiple mechanisms, which depend on heteromerization of A1 and A2A receptors among themselves and with D1 and D2 receptors, respectively. Caffeine produces its motor and reinforcing effects by releasing the pre- and post-synaptic brakes that adenosine imposes on dopaminergic neurotransmission in the SSM. By releasing the pre-synaptic brake, caffeine induces glutamate-dependent and glutamate-independent release of dopamine.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=J.+Neurochem.&amp;rft.atitle=An+update+on+the+mechanisms+of+the+psychostimulant+effects+of+caffeine&amp;rft.volume=105&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.pages=1067-1079&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1111%2Fj.1471-4159.2007.05196.x&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F18088379&amp;rft.aulast=Ferr%C3%A9&amp;rft.aufirst=S&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-pmid20164566-135"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-pmid20164566_135-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Ribeiro JA, Sebastião AM (2010). "Caffeine and adenosine". <i>Journal of Alzheimer's Disease</i>. 20 Suppl 1: S3–15. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.3233%2FJAD-2010-1379" rel="nofollow">10.3233/JAD-2010-1379</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20164566" rel="nofollow">20164566</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Alzheimer%27s+Disease&amp;rft.atitle=Caffeine+and+adenosine&amp;rft.volume=20+Suppl+1&amp;rft.pages=S3-15&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.3233%2FJAD-2010-1379&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F20164566&amp;rft.aulast=Ribeiro&amp;rft.aufirst=JA&amp;rft.au=Sebasti%C3%A3o%2C+AM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-PDEs-Essayan-136"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-PDEs-Essayan_136-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Essayan DM (November 2001). "Cyclic nucleotide phosphodiesterases". <i>The Journal of Allergy and Clinical Immunology</i>. <b>108</b> (5): 671–80. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1067%2Fmai.2001.119555" rel="nofollow">10.1067/mai.2001.119555</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11692087" rel="nofollow">11692087</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Journal+of+Allergy+and+Clinical+Immunology&amp;rft.atitle=Cyclic+nucleotide+phosphodiesterases&amp;rft.volume=108&amp;rft.issue=5&amp;rft.pages=671-80&amp;rft.date=2001-11&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1067%2Fmai.2001.119555&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F11692087&amp;rft.aulast=Essayan&amp;rft.aufirst=DM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-PTX-Deree-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-PTX-Deree_137-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Deree J, Martins JO, Melbostad H, Loomis WH, Coimbra R (June 2008). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2664230" rel="nofollow">"Insights into the regulation of TNF-alpha production in <li id="cite_note-208"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-208">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1819, Runge was invited to show Goethe how belladonna caused dilation of the pupil, which Runge did, using a cat as an experimental subject.  Goethe was so impressed with the demonstration that:  <i>"Nachdem Goethe mir seine größte Zufriedenheit sowol über die Erzählung des durch scheinbaren schwarzen Staar Geretteten, wie auch über das andere ausgesprochen, übergab er mir noch eine Schachtel mit Kaffeebohnen, die ein Grieche ihm als etwas Vorzügliches gesandt. "Auch diese können Sie zu Ihren Untersuchungen brauchen," sagte Goethe.  Er hatte recht; denn bald darauf entdeckte ich darin das, wegen seines großen Stickstoffgehaltes so berühmt gewordene Coffein."</i>  (After Goethe had expressed to me his greatest satisfaction regarding the account of the man [whom I'd] rescued [from serving in Napoleon's army] by apparent "black star" [i.e., amaurosis, blindness] as well as the other, he handed me a carton of coffee beans, which a Greek had sent him as a delicacy.  "You can also use these in your investigations," said Goethe.  He was right; for soon thereafter I discovered therein caffeine, which became so famous on account of its high nitrogen content.)<br/>
This account appeared in Runge's book <i>Hauswirtschaftlichen Briefen</i> (Domestic Letters [i.e., personal correspondence]) of 1866.  It was reprinted in:  Johann Wolfgang von Goethe with F.W. von Biedermann, ed., <i>Goethes Gespräche</i>, vol. 10:  <i>Nachträge, 1755–1832</i> (Leipzig, (Germany):  F.W. v. Biedermann, 1896), pages 89–96; see especially 
<a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=MacwAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA95" rel="nofollow">page 95</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-weinberg-209"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-weinberg_209-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Weinberg BA, Bealer BK (2001). <i>The World of Caffeine: The Science and Culture of the World's Most Popular Drug</i>. Routledge. pp. xvii–xxi. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-415-92723-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-415-92723-9">978-0-415-92723-9</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+World+of+Caffeine%3A+The+Science+and+Culture+of+the+World%27s+Most+Popular+Drug&amp;rft.pages=xvii-xxi&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-415-92723-9&amp;rft.aulast=Weinberg&amp;rft.aufirst=Bennett+Alan&amp;rft.au=Bealer%2C+Bonnie+K.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-210"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-210">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Berzelius, Jöns Jakob (1825). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=XJI8AAAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA1" rel="nofollow">"Jahres-Bericht über die Fortschritte der physischen Wissenschaften von Jacob Berzelius"</a> [Annual report on the progress of the physical sciences by Jacob Berzelius] (in German). <b>4</b>: 180.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Jahres-Bericht+%C3%BCber+die+Fortschritte+der+physischen+Wissenschaften+von+Jacob+Berzelius&amp;rft.volume=4&amp;rft.pages=180&amp;rft.date=1825&amp;rft.aulast=Berzelius&amp;rft.aufirst=J%C3%B6ns+Jakob&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DXJI8AAAAIAAJ%26pg%3DPA1&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>  From page 180:  <i>"Caféin ist eine Materie im Kaffee, die zu gleicher Zeit, 1821, von Robiquet und Pelletier und Caventou entdekt wurde, von denen aber keine etwas darüber im Drucke bekannt machte."</i>  (Caffeine is a material in coffee, which was discovered at the same time, 1821, by Robiquet and [by] Pelletier and Caventou, by whom however nothing was made known about it in the press.)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-211"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-211">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Berzelius JJ (1828). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=iGs1AAAAcAAJ&amp;pag" rel="nofollow"><i>Jahres-Bericht über die Fortschritte der physischen Wissenschaften von Jacob Berzelius</i></a> [<i>Annual Report on the Progress of the Physical Sciences by Jacob Berzelius</i>] (in German). <b>7</b>. p. 270.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Jahres-Bericht+%C3%BCber+die+Fortschritte+der+physischen+Wissenschaften+von+Jacob+Berzelius&amp;rft.pages=270&amp;rft.date=1828&amp;rft.au=Berzelius+JJ&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DiGs1AAAAcAAJ%26pag&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/> From page 270:  <i>"Es darf indessen hierbei nicht unerwähnt bleiben, dass Runge (in seinen phytochemischen Entdeckungen 1820, p. 146-7.) dieselbe Methode angegeben, und das Caffein unter dem Namen </i>Caffeebase<i> ein Jahr eher beschrieben hat, als Robiquet, dem die Entdeckung dieser Substanz gewöhnlich zugeschrieben wird, in einer Zusammenkunft der Societé de Pharmacie in Paris die erste mündliche Mittheilung darüber gab."</i> (However, at this point, it should not remain unmentioned that Runge (in his <i>Phytochemical Discoveries</i>, 1820, pages 146–147) specified the same method and described caffeine under the name <i>Caffeebase</i> a year earlier than Robiquet, to whom the discovery of this substance is usually attributed, having made the first oral announcement about it at a meeting of the Pharmacy Society in Paris.)</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-218"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-218">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Fischer began his studies of caffeine in 1881; however, understanding of the molecule's structure long eluded him.  In 1895 he synthesized caffeine, but only in 1897 did he finally fully determine its molecular structure.
<ul><li><cite class="citation journal">Fischer E (1881). <a class="external text" href="http://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k90692z/f640.image.langEN" rel="nofollow">"Ueber das Caffeïn"</a> [On caffeine]. <i>Berichte der Deutschen Chemischen Gesellschaft zu Berlin</i> (in German). <b>14</b>: 637–644. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1002%2Fcber.188101401142" rel="nofollow">10.1002/cber.188101401142</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Berichte+der+Deutschen+Chemischen+Gesellschaft+zu+Berlin&amp;rft.atitle=Ueber+das+Caffe%C3%AFn&amp;rft.volume=14&amp;rft.pages=637-644&amp;rft.date=1881&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1002%2Fcber.188101401142&amp;rft.au=Fischer+E&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fgallica.bnf.fr%2Fark%3A%2F12148%2Fbpt6k90692z%2Ff640.image.langEN&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaffeine"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></li>
